        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186"><meta property="og:title" content="3D-Printed Sodiophilic V2CTx/rGO-CNT MXene Microgrid Aerogel for Stable Na Metal Anode with High Areal Capacity"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/asset/images/acsnano.2c01186.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="Featuring a high theoretical capacity, low cost, and abundant resources, sodium metal has emerged as an ideal anode material for sodium ion batteries. However, the real feasibility of sodium metal anodes is still hampered by the uncontrolled sodium dendrite problems. Herein, an artificial three-dimensional (3D) hierarchical porous sodiophilic V2CTx/rGO-CNT microgrid aerogel is fabricated by a direct-ink writing 3D printing technology and further adopted as the matrix of Na metal to deliver a Na@V2CTx/rGO-CNT sodium metal anode. Upon cycling, the V2CTx/rGO-CNT electrode can yield a superior cycling life of more than 3000 h (2 mA cm–2, 10 mAh cm–2) with an average Coulombic efficiency of 99.54%. More attractively, it can even sustain a stable operation over 900 h at 5 mA cm–2 with an ultrahigh areal capacity of 50 mAh cm–2. In situ and ex situ characterizations and density functional theory simulation analyses prove that V2CTx with abundant sodiophilic functional groups can effectively guide the sodium metal nucleation and uniform deposition, thus enabling a dendrite-free morphology. Moreover, a full cell pairing a Na@V2CTx/rGO-CNT anode with a Na3V2(PO4)3@C-rGO cathode can deliver a high reversible capacity of 86.27 mAh g–1 after 400 cycles at 100 mA g–1. This work not only clarifies the superior Na deposition chemistry on the sodiophilic V2CTx/rGO-CNT microgrid aerogel electrode but also offers an approach for fabricating advanced Na metal anodes via a 3D printing method."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/asset/images/acsnano.2c01186.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/nwyw~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="90f6ed5b6893775c-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6ed5b6893775c-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: '54d60f0c-6a28-43ce-9036-3a6671bb5ed1'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6ed5b6893775c-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'nano';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/nano/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/nano/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

$(function() {
    var serialCode = "ancac3";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "3D-Printed Sodiophilic V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;CT&lt;sub&gt;&lt;italic toggle&#x3D;&quot;yes&quot;&gt;x&lt;/italic&gt;&lt;/sub&gt;/rGO-CNT MXene Microgrid Aerogel for Stable Na Metal Anode with High Areal Capacity", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.2c01186", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "3D-Printed Sodiophilic V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;CT&lt;sub&gt;&lt;italic toggle&#x3D;&quot;yes&quot;&gt;x&lt;/italic&gt;&lt;/sub&gt;/rGO-CNT MXene Microgrid Aerogel for Stable Na Metal Anode with High Areal Capacity", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.2c01186", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "3D-Printed Sodiophilic V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;CT&lt;sub&gt;&lt;italic toggle&#x3D;&quot;yes&quot;&gt;x&lt;/italic&gt;&lt;/sub&gt;/rGO-CNT MXene Microgrid Aerogel for Stable Na Metal Anode with High Areal Capacity", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.2c01186", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "3D-Printed Sodiophilic V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;CT&lt;sub&gt;&lt;italic toggle&#x3D;&quot;yes&quot;&gt;x&lt;/italic&gt;&lt;/sub&gt;/rGO-CNT MXene Microgrid Aerogel for Stable Na Metal Anode with High Areal Capacity", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.2c01186", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "3D-Printed Sodiophilic V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;CT&lt;sub&gt;&lt;italic toggle&#x3D;&quot;yes&quot;&gt;x&lt;/italic&gt;&lt;/sub&gt;/rGO-CNT MXene Microgrid Aerogel for Stable Na Metal Anode with High Areal Capacity", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.2c01186", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "3D-Printed Sodiophilic V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;CT&lt;sub&gt;&lt;italic toggle&#x3D;&quot;yes&quot;&gt;x&lt;/italic&gt;&lt;/sub&gt;/rGO-CNT MXene Microgrid Aerogel for Stable Na Metal Anode with High Areal Capacity", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.2c01186", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "3D-Printed Sodiophilic V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;CT&lt;sub&gt;&lt;italic toggle&#x3D;&quot;yes&quot;&gt;x&lt;/italic&gt;&lt;/sub&gt;/rGO-CNT MXene Microgrid Aerogel for Stable Na Metal Anode with High Areal Capacity", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.2c01186", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "3D-Printed Sodiophilic V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;CT&lt;sub&gt;&lt;italic toggle&#x3D;&quot;yes&quot;&gt;x&lt;/italic&gt;&lt;/sub&gt;/rGO-CNT MXene Microgrid Aerogel for Stable Na Metal Anode with High Areal Capacity", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.2c01186", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "3D-Printed Sodiophilic V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;CT&lt;sub&gt;&lt;italic toggle&#x3D;&quot;yes&quot;&gt;x&lt;/italic&gt;&lt;/sub&gt;/rGO-CNT MXene Microgrid Aerogel for Stable Na Metal Anode with High Areal Capacity", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsnano.2c01186", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

Empty dropzone --></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="_i1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/asset/images/medium/nn2c01186_0007.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/asset/images/large/nn2c01186_0007.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.2c01186&amp;id=_i1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">Featuring a high theoretical capacity, low cost, and abundant resources, sodium metal has emerged as an ideal anode material for sodium ion batteries. However, the real feasibility of sodium metal anodes is still hampered by the uncontrolled sodium dendrite problems. Herein, an artificial three-dimensional (3D) hierarchical porous sodiophilic V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT microgrid aerogel is fabricated by a direct-ink writing 3D printing technology and further adopted as the matrix of Na metal to deliver a Na@V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT sodium metal anode. Upon cycling, the V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT electrode can yield a superior cycling life of more than 3000 h (2 mA cm<sup>–2</sup>, 10 mAh cm<sup>–2</sup>) with an average Coulombic efficiency of 99.54%. More attractively, it can even sustain a stable operation over 900 h at 5 mA cm<sup>–2</sup> with an ultrahigh areal capacity of 50 mAh cm<sup>–2</sup>. <i>In situ</i> and <i>ex</i><i>situ</i> characterizations and density functional theory simulation analyses prove that V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub> with abundant sodiophilic functional groups can effectively guide the sodium metal nucleation and uniform deposition, thus enabling a dendrite-free morphology. Moreover, a full cell pairing a Na@V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT anode with a Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>@C-rGO cathode can deliver a high reversible capacity of 86.27 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 400 cycles at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. This work not only clarifies the superior Na deposition chemistry on the sodiophilic V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT microgrid aerogel electrode but also offers an approach for fabricating advanced Na metal anodes <i>via</i> a 3D printing method.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D9105%26pageCount%3D12%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DZixuan%2BWang%252C%2BZhenxin%2BHuang%252C%2BHui%2BWang%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D16%26issueNum%3D6%26contentID%3Dacsnano.2c01186%26title%3D3D-Printed%2BSodiophilic%2BV2CTx%252FrGO-CNT%2BMXene%2BMicrogrid%2BAerogel%2Bfor%2BStable%2BNa%2BMetal%2BAnode%2Bwith%2BHigh%2BAreal%2BCapacity%26numPages%3D12%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1936-0851%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Dancac3%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D9116%26publicationDate%3DJune%2B2022" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2022 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292505&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Aerogels" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Aerogels" class="article__tags__link">Aerogels</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290743&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Deposition" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Deposition" class="article__tags__link">Deposition</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrodes" class="article__tags__link">Electrodes</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290797&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Metals" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Metals" class="article__tags__link">Metals</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292522&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Two dimensional materials" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Two%20dimensional%20materials" class="article__tags__link">Two dimensional materials</a></li></ul></div></div></div></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--keywords hlFld-Abstract"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=V2ctx+Mxene&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_V2CTx%20MXene">V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub> MXene</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium+Metal+Anode&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_sodium%20metal%20anode">sodium metal anode</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=3D+Printing&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_3D%20printing">3D printing</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=High+Areal+Capacity&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_high%20areal%20capacity">high areal capacity</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Dendrite-free+Morphology&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_dendrite-free%20morphology">dendrite-free morphology</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="NLM_p first">By virtue of high theoretical capacity (1166 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>), low redox potential (−2.71 V <i>vs</i> standard hydrogen electrode), high abundance, and low cost, sodium metal is considered to be an ideal anode for sodium ion batteries (SIBs). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4 ref5 ref6'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4 ref5 ref6" aria-label="reference 1 to 6">(1−6)</a> However, the low Coulombic efficiency (CE), rapid capacity attenuation, and even safety problems caused by the uncontrolled growth of sodium dendrites during the repeated plating/stripping process still limit its practical applications. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7 ref8 ref9'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref7 ref8 ref9" aria-label="reference 7 to 9">(7−9)</a> To tackle these issues, burgeoning efforts have been proposed, such as electrolyte modification, artificial interface engineering, alloying design, and 3D nanostructure scaffold matrix manipulation. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1 ref10 ref11 ref12 ref13 ref14 ref15 ref16'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref10 ref11 ref12 ref13 ref14 ref15 ref16" aria-label="reference 1 and 10 to 16">(1,10−16)</a> Despite much progress have been achieved with these smart strategies, pursuing an efficient Na metal matrix fabricated by advanced technology is still an imperative need to obtain high-performance Na metal anodes with high areal capacity and long cycling stability.</div><div class="NLM_p">As a special group of two-dimensional layered material, MXene has attracted extensive attention and research interest as a Na metal matrix owing to its high electrical conductivity, abundant surface groups, hydrophilicity, and high mechanical modulus. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17 ref18 ref19 ref20 ref21 ref22'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref17 ref18 ref19 ref20 ref21 ref22" aria-label="reference 17 to 22">(17−22)</a> Some pioneer works, such as a three-dimensional (3D) porous Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>-rGO membrane (rGO = reduced graphene oxide), <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23" aria-label="reference 23">(23)</a> Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>-modified carbon cloth (Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>-CC), <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3" aria-label="reference 3">(3)</a> pillared Sn@MXene, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref24" aria-label="reference 24">(24)</a> 3D hydroxylated MXene/carbon nanotubes (h-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>/CNTs), <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25" aria-label="reference 25">(25)</a> 3D Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub>X</sub> MXene-melamine foam, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26" aria-label="reference 26">(26)</a> rGO/MXene hybrid film, and MXene-derived 1D/2D hybrid nanoarchitectures have been designed and employed as the matrix for Na metal anodes. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4 ref27'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref4 ref27" aria-label="reference 4 and 27">(4,27)</a> Among them, a 3D h-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>/CNTs electrode achieves a high average CE of 99.20% without dendrite formation after 1000 cycles and an ultralong lifespan over 4000 h at a current density of 1 mA cm<sup>–2</sup> with a capacity of 1 mAh cm<sup>–2</sup>. The excellent performances are due to the presence of sodiophilic functional groups of h-Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>, which would greatly promote Na nucleation uniformity and accelerate Na-ion/electron transport kinetics. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25" aria-label="reference 25">(25)</a> Although Na dendrite formation is effectively restrained at the limited current density and areal capacity (for example, 3 mA cm<sup>–2</sup> with 3 mAh cm<sup>–2</sup>), fabricating an electrode that could stand tougher testing conditions at larger capacity and higher current density is still a challenge due to the unsatisfactory electrode architecture design. Additionally, most recent works are focused on Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub> (or Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub><i>x</i></sub>) and related hybrid structures, and other MXenes are seldomly exploited as the matrix of Na metal anodes. Therefore, it is timely and necessary to establish a deeper understanding of the Na deposition behavior onto alternative MXene-derived hybrid structures.</div><div class="NLM_p last">Among various MXene materials, V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub> MXene exhibits high electrochemical activity and promising ion conductivity, which is suitable as a matrix for Na metal. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28 ref29'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref29" aria-label="reference 28 and 29">(28,29)</a> Guided by these merits, a V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT microgrid aerogel electrode is successfully constructed by the 3D printing technology with favorable porous macroporous hierarchical structure. This 3D-printed V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT microgrid is demonstrated to be a superior matrix for Na metal anodes evidenced by the following merits: (1) the large specific surface area can profoundly reduce current density and provide abundant nucleation centers for Na deposition; (2) the 3D-printed artificial hierarchical porous structure not only promotes electrolyte penetration to ensure close contact between the electrolyte and active materials but also greatly improves the ion transport rate and alleviates electrode volume expansion; (3) sodiophilic V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub> MXene nanoflakes with a high binding energy with Na ions can effectively improve the Na nucleation and deposition stability, as verified by <i>in situ</i> transmission electron microscopy (TEM), <i>ex situ</i> scanning electron microscopy (SEM), <i>in situ</i> optical microscopy, and density functional theory (DFT) simulation results. With these advantages, the as-synthesized V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT microgrid electrode can be stably cycled more than 3000 h at 2 mA cm<sup>–2</sup> with 10 mAh cm<sup>–2</sup>, with a high average CE of 99.54%. In addition, even at a large capacity of 50 mAh cm<sup>–2</sup> at 5 mA cm<sup>–2</sup>, a long cycling life of more than 900 h is attained. Furthermore, a full battery assembled with a Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>@C-rGO (NVP@C-rGO) cathode and a Na@V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT anode can yield a high reversible capacity of 86.27 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 100 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. All of these comprehensive analyses build a deep insight into the fabrication of a sodiophilic MXene matrix <i>via</i> the advanced 3D printing technology for boosting the cycling stability of Na metal anodes.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">The preparation process of the 3D-printed V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT anode can be divided into four steps: etching and exfoliation of V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub> MXene nanoflakes, ink preparation, 3D printing of the microgrid hydrogel, and post-treatment (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a>). Figure S1a (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/suppl_file/nn2c01186_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>) shows the typical morphology of the V<sub>2</sub>AlC MAX powder in micrometer size with rough surfaces. Upon etching by HF acid at 50 °C, V<sub>2</sub>AlC was converted into multilayer V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub> MXene by etching away the interlayer of Al atoms (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/suppl_file/nn2c01186_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1b</a>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30" aria-label="reference 30">(30)</a> Subsequently, the multilayers can be exfoliated into single or few layers by raising the pH value close to neutral, followed by mixing with tetrabutylammonium hydroxide (TBAOH) and ultrasonic mechanical vibration (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/suppl_file/nn2c01186_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1c</a>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref31" aria-label="reference 31">(31)</a> During the etching process, plenty of oxygen-containing and fluorine-containing functional groups were generated on the surface of the MXene nanosheets, which is the origin of the hydrophilicity and sodiophilicity of the MXene nanoflakes. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23 ref32 ref33 ref34 ref35'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23 ref32 ref33 ref34 ref35" aria-label="reference 23 and 32 to 35">(23,32−35)</a> In this work, V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub> MXene nanoflakes with an average size of about 30 nm were used as the active materials incorporated with a GO-CNT aqueous slurry to prepare the 3D-printed ink (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 1</a> and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/suppl_file/nn2c01186_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2</a>). It is worth mentioning that there are no additional additives (binders and surfactants) in the prepared printing ink. After filling the prepared slurry into the syringe, the V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/GO-CNT ink with the designed microgrid pattern was printed onto a piece of glass slide substrate layer by layer at room temperature by a direct-ink-writing (DIW) 3D printer system. Subsequently, the 3D-printed V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/GO-CNT microgrid hydrogel was freeze-dried to remove the water to form the aerogel, followed by annealing in an Ar gas environment to convert GO into rGO. CNT and rGO not only provide a strong mechanical scaffold to support V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub> MXene but also accelerate the charge accessibility. According to our previous studies, the addition of CNT can further increase the surface area to reduce the local current density, improve the conductivity to enhance the surface kinetics, and reinforce the electrode structure mechanical strength without fracture or collapse for long-term plating/stripping cycling stability. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36 ref37'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref36 ref37" aria-label="reference 36 and 37">(36,37)</a> The thickness of the 3D-printed V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT microgrid aerogel can be well regulated by controlling the printed layers (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/suppl_file/nn2c01186_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3a</a>). In our experiment, the V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT microgrid aerogel with a size of 1 × 1 cm (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/suppl_file/nn2c01186_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3b</a>) and a thickness of ∼1.5 mm (4 layers) was used for further characterization and as the matrix of Na metal.</div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/asset/images/medium/nn2c01186_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/asset/images/large/nn2c01186_0001.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. Schematic diagram of the preparation process of a 3D-printed V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT microgrid aerogel electrode.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/asset/images/large/nn2c01186_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.2c01186&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">In order to optimize the electrochemical performance, various mass ratios of V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub> (0–50%) in the whole V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT microgrid electrodes were tuned and fabricated. <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/suppl_file/nn2c01186_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S4</a> and <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>a–f show the morphology of the 3D-printed rGO-CNT and 30% V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT microgrid aerogel, respectively. The 3D-printed 30% V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO–CNT microgrid aerogel is composed of well-aligned cross-linked filaments with an average diameter of 150 μm and periodic sub-millimeter channels with an average size of approximately 150 μm (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>a). The printed filaments are composed of rGO nanoflakes, randomly distributed CNT, and plenty of microcavities (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>b,c). Tiny V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub> nanoflakes with an average transverse diameter of 30 nm can be carefully found and randomly distributed on the surface of the rGO-CNT skeleton (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>c,d). The lattice fringes of 0.22 and 0.34 nm correspond to the (002) crystal plane of V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub> and (002) crystal plane of CNT and rGO, respectively (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>e). The rGO-CNT aerogel and 10% and 50% V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT aerogels exhibit a similar morphology with a hierarchical porous structure as shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/suppl_file/nn2c01186_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S4–S6</a>, respectively. In addition, the 3D-printed V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT microgrid aerogel is well stacked, and the V, C, F, and O elements are uniformly distributed over the whole printed microgrid aerogel, as shown from the energy dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDS) elemental mapping in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>f. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>g shows the X-ray diffractometer (XRD) patterns of V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub> and 3D V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT. There is an obvious diffraction peak at 25.32° and a small peak located at 42°, corresponding to the (002) and (100) planes of the carbon matrix (rGO-CNT), respectively. Similarly, the diffraction peak at 7.25° corresponds to the (002) plane of V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref38" aria-label="reference 38">(38)</a> The surface functional groups of V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub> MXene and 3D V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT are characterized by X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) measurement, as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>h and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/suppl_file/nn2c01186_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7</a>. In the V 2p spectrum of 3D V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT, there are two doublet peaks, which can be assigned to V<sup>2+</sup> (V 2p<sub>3/2</sub> 513.46 eV and V 2p<sub>1/2</sub> 521.23 eV) and V<sup>4+</sup> (V 2p<sub>3/2</sub> 516.32 eV and V 2p<sub>1/2</sub> 523.86 eV), as shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/suppl_file/nn2c01186_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7a</a>. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28 ref31 ref39'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref31 ref39" aria-label="reference 28, 31 and 39">(28,31,39)</a> The spectrum of C 1s is composed of three peaks located at 288.18, 284.85, and 282.04 eV, corresponding to C═O, C–C, and V–C bonds, respectively (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/suppl_file/nn2c01186_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7b</a>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28 ref40 ref41'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref28 ref40 ref41" aria-label="reference 28, 40 and 41">(28,40,41)</a> The O 1s peaks at 530.32, 531.53, and 533.53 eV can be attributed to V–O, O–C, and −OH bonds, respectively (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/suppl_file/nn2c01186_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7c</a>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40 ref42'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref40 ref42" aria-label="reference 40 and 42">(40,42)</a> The F 1s peak at 685.38 eV corresponds to the F–V bond (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/suppl_file/nn2c01186_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S7d</a>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29 ref43'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29 ref43" aria-label="reference 29 and 43">(29,43)</a> XPS spectra of V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT nanosheets confirm the presence of hydrophilic −O and −F functional groups on the surface. The ratio of V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub> in the nanocomposites is further determined by the thermogravimetric analysis (TGA) results, as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 2</a>i and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/suppl_file/nn2c01186_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S1</a>, which is agreed well with the initial ratios. From the TGA curves, the weight loss between 100 and 530 °C is attributed to the oxidation of rGO and CNT. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref44" aria-label="reference 44">(44)</a> The weight increase of V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT composites after 530 °C is attributed to the conversion of V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub> to VO<sub><i>x</i></sub> (mixture of V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub>, V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, VO<sub>2</sub>, and V<sub>3</sub>O<sub>7</sub>), as shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/suppl_file/nn2c01186_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S8</a>. In addition, the specific surface areas of rGO-CNT and 10%, 30%, and 50% V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT electrodes are 353.08, 192.7, 164.49, and 98.44 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively, and the related pore sizes are 4.45, 14.32, 16.72, and 14.67 nm, respectively (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/suppl_file/nn2c01186_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S9</a>).</div><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/asset/images/medium/nn2c01186_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/asset/images/large/nn2c01186_0002.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. SEM images of (a–c) the 30% V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT microgrid aerogel. (d) TEM and (e) HRTEM images of V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT nanocomposites. (f) SEM of the V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT microgrid aerogel cross section and corresponding EDS elemental mapping. (g) XRD patterns of rGO-CNT, V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>, and V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT nanocomposites. (h) XPS spectra of V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub> MXene and V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT. (i) TGA curves of rGO-CNT and V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT nanocomposites.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/asset/images/large/nn2c01186_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.2c01186&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The electrochemical performances of the 3D V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT electrodes are summarized in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>. As shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>a, when measured at a current density of 2 mA cm<sup>–2</sup> with a capacity of 1 mAh cm<sup>–2</sup>, the initial CE of 2D planar Cu foil is only 69.24%, and the CE fluctuated in the range of 61.91–100% from the second to the 346th cycle. The unstable CE is mainly caused by uneven Na ion deposition and the formed unstable solid-electrolyte interface (SEI) film. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34 ref45 ref46'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref34 ref45 ref46" aria-label="reference 34, 45 and 46">(34,45,46)</a> In contrast, rGO-CNT, 10% V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT, 30% V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT, and 50% V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT electrodes exhibit much more stable CEs and longer lifespans (600, 1300, and 400 cycles for rGO-CNT, 10% V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT, and 50% V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT, respectively). Moreover, 30% V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT exhibits the stablest cycle performance with the highest CE. For example, the CE of 30% V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT is 79.16% at the first cycle, and it increased rapidly to 98.00% at the third cycle and stabilized with an average CE of 99.35% in the following approximately 1700 cycles. The rate performance of various electrodes is measured at the current densities varied from 0.5 to 8 mA cm<sup>–2</sup> with a fixed plating/stripping duration of 1 h, as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>b. The 2D planar Cu foil is short-circuited even when measured at 0.5 mA cm<sup>–2</sup>, and the related overpotential is 39.5 mV (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/suppl_file/nn2c01186_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S10a</a>). It is still observed that the 3D-printed microgrid electrodes exhibit a much better rate capability than 2D planar Cu foil electrodes. When the current densities are 0.5, 1, 2, 4, 5, and 8 mA cm<sup>–2</sup>, the nucleation overpotentials of rGO-CNT are 14.6, 20.2, 25.1, 27.6, 30.2, and 40.3 mV, respectively (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>c). The nucleation overpotentials of 30% V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT are 9.6, 13.3, 16.2, 20.1, 22.6, and 29.2 mV, respectively (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>d). As shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 3</a>e and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/suppl_file/nn2c01186_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S2</a>, 30% V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT exhibits the lowest nucleation overpotentials compared with other electrodes. This result demonstrates that the 30% V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT anode exhibits the best rate performance, which can be attributed to the rational 3D-printed hierarchical structure and optimized V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub> content, the enabled fast ion/electron transport kinetics, and uniform Na ion deposition. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47 ref48 ref49'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref47 ref48 ref49" aria-label="reference 47 to 49">(47−49)</a> The surface kinetics were investigated by exploring the charge transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>) and the diffusion coefficient (<i>D</i>) derived from the electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS). As shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/suppl_file/nn2c01186_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S11a</a>, the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of rGO-CNT and 10%, 30%, and 50% V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT electrodes before cycling are 109.55, 104.31, 79.00, and 27.22 Ω, respectively. After 50 cycles, they are decreased to 66.29, 54.99, 10.83, and 21.87 Ω, respectively (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/suppl_file/nn2c01186_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S11b</a> and <a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">Table 1</a>). The results indicate that <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> decreases significantly with the addition of V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>. At the same time, the diffusion coefficient of 30% V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT is 6.67 × 10<sup>–14</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> S<sup>–1</sup>, which is the highest among these 3D-printed electrodes (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/suppl_file/nn2c01186_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S11c</a> and <a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">Table 1</a>). However, when the V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub> ratio is higher than 30%, the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> is increased; the reason may be due to the limited surface area of 50% V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT (98.44 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>–1</sup>) and reduced pore size, leading to the slower charge transfer rate (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/suppl_file/nn2c01186_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S11</a>). <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref49'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref49" aria-label="reference 49">(49)</a> The above results demonstrate that the 30% V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT microgrid aerogel with the optimized amount of V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub> exhibits accelerated charge transfer speeds and enhanced surface kinetics.</div><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/asset/images/medium/nn2c01186_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/asset/images/large/nn2c01186_0003.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. Electrochemical performance of Na metal plating/stripping on 2D planar Cu foil, rGO-CNT, and various V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT electrodes. (a) CE of the electrode at 2 mA cm<sup>–2</sup> with 1 mAh cm<sup>–2</sup>. (b) Rate performance of various electrodes at current densities ranging from 0.5 to 8 mA cm<sup>–2</sup> with a limited plating/stripping duration of 1 h. The inset in (b) shows the short circuit of the Cu foil electrode. Voltage–capacity curves of (c) rGO-CNT and (d) 30% V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT microgrid electrodes at various current densities measured in (b). (e) Nucleation overpotentials of each electrode at various current densities measured in (b). Cycle performance of the 30% V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT electrode at (f) 2 mA cm<sup>–2</sup> with 10 mAh cm<sup>–2</sup> and (g) 5 mA cm<sup>–2</sup> with 50 mAh cm<sup>–2</sup>. Radar charts of the electrochemical performance comparison of (h) 3D-printed graphene-based matrices for Na metal anodes and (i) various MXene-based Na metal anodes.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsnano.2c01186/asset/images/large/nn2c01186_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsnano.2c01186&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_table-wrap" id="tbl1"><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption"><div class="NLM_caption" id=""><div class="title2">Table 1. Comparison of Charge Transfer Resistance, Warburg Impedance, and Diffusion Coefficient of Sodium Ions for Various Electrodes after 50 Cycles</div></div></div><div class="scrollable-table-wrap"><table class="table "><colgroup><col align="left"><col align="char" char="."><col align="char" char="."><col align="char" char="×"></colgroup><thead><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center">electrode</th><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center" char="."><i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> (Ω)</th><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center" char=".">σ</th><th class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="col" align="center" char="×"><i>D</i> (cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>–1</sup>)</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">3D rGO-CNT</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">66.29</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">15.16</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub><i>x</i></sub>/rGO-CNT</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">54.99</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">12.8</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0"
