            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metallic anodes have high theor. specific capacities and low electrochem. potentials.  However, short-circuit problems caused by dendritic deposition and low Coulombic efficiency limit the cyclic life and safety of metallic anode-based batteries.  Herein, dendrite-free and flexible three-dimensional (3D) alkali anodes (Li/Na-Ti3C2Tx-rGO) are constructed by infusing molten lithium (Li) or sodium (Na) metal into 3D porous MXene Ti3C2Tx-reduced graphene oxide (Ti3C2Tx-rGO) membranes.  First-principles calcns. indicate that large fractions of functional groups on the Ti3C2Tx surface lead to the good affinity between the Ti3C2Tx-rGO membrane and molten alkali metal (Li/Na), and the formation of Ti-Li/Na, O-Li/Na, and F-Li/Na mixed covalent/ionic bonds is extremely crit. for uniform electrochem. deposition.  Furthermore, the porous structure in Li/Na-Ti3C2Tx-rGO composites results in an effective encapsulation, preventing dendritic growth and exhibiting stable stripping/plating behaviors up to 12 mA·cm-2 and a deeper capacity of 10 mA·h·cm-2.  Stable cycling performances over 300 h (750 cycles) at 5.0 mA·cm-2 for Li-Ti3C2Tx-rGO and 500 h (750 cycles) at 3.0 mA·cm-2 for Na-Ti3C2Tx-GO are achieved.  In a full cell with LiFePO4 cathodes, Li-Ti3C2Tx-rGO electrodes show low polarization and retain 96.6% capacity after 1000 cycles.  These findings are based on 2D MXene materials, and the resulting 3D host provides a practical approach for achieving stable and safe alkali metal anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGouMt50nb3RD7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhCfKv44ILAHg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitF2ntb%252FK&amp;md5=284a202fbe95875803b3978f5462999b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201805946"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Matios, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Pillared MXene with Ultralarge Interlayer Spacing as a Stable Matrix for High Performance Sodium Metal Anodes</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A 3D Hydroxylated MXene/Carbon Nanotubes Composite as a Scaffold for Dendrite-Free Sodium-Metal Electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Xin; Jin, Song; Miao, Licheng; Cai, Yichao; Hou, Yunpeng; Li, Haixia; Zhang, Kai; Yan, Zhenhua; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium metal is a promising anode, but uneven Na deposition with a dendrite growth seriously impedes its application.  Herein, a fibrous hydroxylated MXene/carbon nanotubes (h-Ti3C2/CNTs) composite is designed as a scaffold for dendrite-free Na metal electrodes.  This composite displays fast Na+/electron transport kinetics and good thermal cond. and mech. properties.  The h-Ti3C2 contains abundant sodiophilic functional groups, which play a significant role in inducing homogeneous nucleation of Na.  Meanwhile, CNTs provide high tensile strength and ease of film-forming.  As a result, h-Ti3C2/CNTs exhibit a high av. Coulombic efficiency of 99.2% and no dendrite after 1000 cycles.  The h-Ti3C2/CNTs/Na based sym. cells show a long lifespan over 4000 h at 1.0 mA cm-2 with a capacity of 1.0 mAh cm-2.  Furthermore, Na-O2 batteries with a h-Ti3C2/CNTs/Na anode exhibit a low potential gap of 0.11 V after an initial 70 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrUVbo66t12QLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhWyG6wy61ACw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsVakur7I&amp;md5=8bf835b3001371f326c8ef15bc93b3e1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.0c03042"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yue, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, C.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">3D Flexible, Conductive, and Recyclable Ti3C2Tx MXene-Melamine Foam for High-Areal-Capacity and Long-Lifetime Alkali-Metal Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shi, Haodong; Yue, Meng; Zhang, Chuanfang John; Dong, Yanfeng; Lu, Pengfei; Zheng, Shuanghao; Huang, Huijuan; Chen, Jie; Wen, Pengchao; Xu, Zhaochao; Zheng, Qiong; Li, Xianfeng; Yu, Yan; Wu, Zhong-Shuai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8678-8688</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Alkali metals are ideal anodes for high-energy-d. rechargeable batteries, while seriously hampered by limited cycle life and low areal capacities.  To this end, rationally designed frameworks for dendrite-free and vol.-changeless alkali-metal deposition at both high current densities and capacities are urgently required.  Herein, a general 3D conductive Ti3C2TX MXene-melamine foam (MXene-MF) is demonstrated as an elastic scaffold for dendrite-free, high-areal-capacity alkali anodes (Li, Na, K).  Owing to the lithiophilic nature of F-terminated MXene, conductive macroporous network, and excellent mech. toughness, the constructed MXene-MF synchronously achieves a high c.d. of 50 mA cm-2 for Li plating, high areal capacity (50 mAh cm-2) with high Coulombic efficiency (99%), and long lifetime (3800 h), surpassing the Li anodes reported recently.  Meanwhile, MXene-MF shows flat voltage profiles for 720 h at 10 mA cm-2 for the Na anode and 800 h at 5 mA cm-2 for the K anode, indicative of the wide applicability.  Notably, the high c.d. of 20 mA cm-2 for 20 mAh cm-2 for the Na anode, accompanying good recyclability was rarely achieved before.  When coupled with sulfur or Na3V2(PO4)3 cathodes, the assembled MXene-MF alkali (Li, Na)-based full batteries showcase enhanced rate capability and cycling stability, demonstrating the potential of MXene-MF for advanced alkali-metal batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrCgv2nPPQTirVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhWyG6wy61ACw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Engineering rGO/MXene Hybrid Film as an Anode Host for Stable Sodium-Metal Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Shiyang; Liu, Yang; Lu, Ke; Cai, Wenbin; Jie, Yulin; Huang, Fanyang; Li, Xinpeng; Cao, Ruiguo; Jiao, Shuhong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Fuels</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium metal batteries have attracted extensive attentions due to their high energy d. and low-cost resources.  However, the realization of Na metal anodes is still hampered by intrinsic Na dendrite growth and uncontrollable volumetric expansion.  Herein, a hybrid rGO/MXene film is fabricated via a filtration and spark approach, which is used as a sodiophilic anode host for stabilizing sodium-metal anode.  The surface-attached MXene nanosheets could regulate the sodium deposition behavior and suppress dendrite growth, while the reduced graphene oxide scaffold provide the efficient electron transport pathways.  As a result, the designed Na@rGO/MXene electrode shows excellent electrochem. performance in terms of high Coulombic efficiency, low deposition overpotential, and long-term cycling stability.  Moreover, a Na3V2(PO4)3||Na full cell with a low N/P ratio of 3.8 is realized, showing great opportunities for practical sodium-metal batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr0a5zzkN1ziLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhWyG6wy61ACw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Superior-Performance Aqueous Zinc-Ion Batteries Based on the In Situ Growth of MnO2 Nanosheets on V2CTX MXene</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Xiaodong; Cao, Ziyi; Wang, Wenjie; Li, Haijing; Dong, Juncai; Gao, Shangpeng; Xu, Dongxiao; Li, Lei; Shen, Jianfeng; Ye, Mingxin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2971-2983</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Mn-based aq. zinc-ion batteries (ZIBs) are promising candidate for large-scale rechargeable energy storage because of easy fabrication, low cost, and high safety.  Nevertheless, the com. application of Mn-based cathode is hindered by the challenging issues of low rate capability and poor cyclability.  Herein, a manganese-vanadium hybrid, K-V2C@MnO2 cathode, featured with MnO2 nanosheets uniformly formed on a V2CTX MXene surface, is elaborately designed and synthesized by metal-cation intercalation and following in situ growth strategy.  Benefiting from the hybrid structure with high cond., abundant active sites, and the synergistic reaction of Mn2+ electrodeposition and inhibited structural damage of MnO2, K-V2C@MnO2 shows excellent electrochem. performance for aq. ZIBs.  Specifically, it presents the high specific capacity of 408.1 mAh g-1 at 0.3 A g-1 and maintains the specific capacity of 119.2 mAh g-1 at a high c.d. of 10 A g-1 in a long-term cycle of up to 10000 cycles.  It is superior to almost all reported Mn-based cathodes for ZIBs in the aq. electrolyte.  The superior electrochem. performance suggests that the Mn-based cathode materials designed in this work can be a rational approach to be applied for high-performance ZIBs cathodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoSIASqFdyFRLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lguMg4YIYnrGg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXhvVyisrs%253D&amp;md5=8e928c7add0adf858c237d54a68865ca</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1039/D0TA04506C"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Interstratification-assembled 2D black phosphorene and V2CTx MXene as superior anodes for boosting potassium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Xinming; Wang, Han; Zhao, Zhilin; Huang, Bin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">25</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">12705-12715</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Although potassium-ion batteries have been widely studied because of their low cost and high theor. capacity, the origin of the poor potassium-ion storage kinetics and low structural stability still remains elusive mainly due to the large size of K+ (0.138 nm).  Herein, we report an interstratification-assembly strategy via van der Waals interactions to design a novel BPE@V2CTx hybrid anode, wherein black phosphorene (BPE) and V2CTx MXene are derived from their individual 2D nanosheets.  The coupled BPE@V2CTx hybrid anode with a 2D stacked interstratification structure and large sp. surface area could efficiently take advantage of BPE and V2CTx nanosheets and create more active sites.  This interstratification hybrid electrode not only provides an enlarged interlayer spacing and a three-dimensional interconnected conductive network to accelerate the K+ transport rates, but also has good tolerance to vol. changes caused by phase transformations during the fast potassiation/depotassiation process.  DFT calcns. further confirm that potassium affinities and diffusion kinetics are significantly enhanced in the BPE@V2CTx hybrid anode, particularly in BPE@V2CF2.  As a result, the hybrid anode possesses a remarkable synergetic effect and achieves a high reversible capacity of 593.6 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1 and excellent cycling stability of 485/261 mA h g-1 with 91/86% capacity retention after 3000 cycles at 0.2/2.0 A g-1.  This work opens a new way for the application of self-assembled hybrid electrodes in energy storage, electrocatalysis and sensors.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpNvZ-xifw7S7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lguMg4YIYnrGg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhtFahsbvK&amp;md5=304c5777d2603a3d67cadeca7aa1a224</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201700959"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bak, S.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Stretchable Zn-Ion Hybrid Battery with Reconfigurable V2CTx and Ti3C2Tx MXene Electrodes as a Magnetically Actuated Soft Robot</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yang; Yang, Haitao; Zhang, Tianran; Li, Shuo; Li, Shuai; He, Shuaiming; Chen, Tianle; Lee, Jim Yang; Zhao, Yusheng; Chen, Po-Yen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">45</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2101862</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Stretchable energy storage devices have become indispensable components toward energy autonomy for wearable electronic, implantable medical devices, and untethered soft machines.  A Zn-based battery with a neutral electrolyte could act as a competitive candidate for wearable/implantable electronics because of its intrinsic safety and high energy d.  Therefore, it is highly desired to develop a synergistic combination of stretchable anodes/cathodes and neutral electrolytes for stretchable Zn-based batteries.  Herein, a scalable fabrication process is developed to produce stretchable Zn-ion hybrid batteries composed of V2CTx MXene cathodes and zinc-decorated Ti3C2Tx MXene anodes.  To endow high stretchability to the Zn-ion hybrid battery, both MXene-based electrodes are fabricated with crumple-like microtextures enabling reversible folding/unfolding behaviors to attenuate in-plane stress while stretching.  In comparison with the state-of-the-art work, the as-fabricated Zn-ion hybrid battery features large deformability (50% strain), ultrathin device (≈170 μm), low areal wt. (≈20 mg cm-2), and an ultralow self-discharge rate (0.7 mV h-2), and demonstrates rechargeable and strain-insensitive specific capacities of 118.5 and 103.6 mAh g-2 under 0% and 50% strains, resp.  Finally, with ultrathin and lightwt. merits, the stretchable battery is further fabricated into a magnetically actuated soft robot with remote control, capable of crawling between two designated points for charging/discharging tasks.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrVyiEQFJzUF7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lguMg4YIYnrGg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXit1eru77F&amp;md5=465b89e2d134e207578bcf8b1ea82ae8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms2664"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mashtalir, O.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Naguib, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mochalin, V. Commun.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>4</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1716</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/ncomms2664</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D4%26publication_year%3D2013%26pages%3D1716%26journal%3DNat.%2BCommun.%26author%3DO.%2BMashtalir%26author%3DM.%2BNaguib%26author%3DV.%2BN.%2BMochalin%26author%3DY.%2BDall%25E2%2580%2599Agnese%26author%3DM.%2BHeon%26author%3DM.%2BW.%2BBarsoum%26author%3DY.%2BGogotsi%26title%3DIntercalation%2Band%2Bdelamination%2Bof%2Blayered%2Bcarbides%2Band%2Bcarbonitrides%26doi%3D10.1038%252Fncomms2664&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.2c01186&amp;doiOfLink=10.1038%2Fncomms2664&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Intercalation and delamination of layered carbides and carbonitrides</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mashtalir Olha; Naguib Michael; Mochalin Vadym N; Dall'Agnese Yohan; Heon Min; Barsoum Michel W; Gogotsi Yury</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1716</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Intercalation and delamination of two-dimensional solids in many cases is a requisite step for exploiting their unique properties.  Herein we report on the intercalation of two-dimensional Ti3C2, Ti3CN and TiNbC-so called MXenes.  Intercalation of hydrazine, and its co-intercalation with N,N-dimethylformamide, resulted in increases of the c-lattice parameters of surface functionalized f-Ti3C2, from 19.5 to 25.48 and 26.8 ÅA, respectively.  Urea is also intercalated into f-Ti3C2.  Molecular dynamics simulations suggest that a hydrazine monolayer intercalates between f-Ti3C2 layers.  Hydrazine is also intercalated into f-Ti3CN and f-TiNbC.  When dimethyl sulphoxide is intercalated into f-Ti3C2, followed by sonication in water, the f-Ti3C2 is delaminated forming a stable colloidal solution that is in turn filtered to produce MXene 'paper'.  The latter shows excellent Li-ion capacity at extremely high charging rates.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcQzZ-BvcJeO7tenUz0lpNqnfW6udTcc2eYzEN49C12Serntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC3srlvVOnuw%253D%253D&amp;md5=d2353c4d0005aa57aeff161518f98e51</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.9b07710"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, C. J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dong, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Z.                 10.1021/acsnano.9b07710</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D13%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D14308-14318%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DH.%2BShi%26author%3DC.%2BJ.%2BZhang%26author%3DP.%2BLu%26author%3DY.%2BDong%26author%3DP.%2BWen%26author%3DZ.%2BS.%2BWu%26title%3DConducting%2Band%2BLithiophilic%2BMXene%252FGraphene%2BFramework%2Bfor%2BHigh-Capacity%252C%2BDendrite-Free%2BLithium-Metal%2BAnodes%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsnano.9b07710&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.2c01186&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsnano.9b07710&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Conducting and Lithiophilic MXene/Graphene Framework for High-Capacity, Dendrite-Free Lithium-Metal Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shi, Haodong; Zhang, Chuanfang John; Lu, Pengfei; Dong, Yanfeng; Wen, Pengchao; Wu, Zhong-Shuai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">14308-14318</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Li-metal anode is widely acknowledged as the ideal anode for high-energy-d. batteries, but seriously hindered by the uncontrollable dendrite growth and infinite vol. change.  Toward this goal, suitable stable scaffolds for dendrite-free Li anodes with large c.d. (&gt;5 mA cm-2) and high Li loading (&gt;90%) are highly in demand.  Herein, a conductive and lithiophilic three-dimensional (3D) MXene/graphene (MG) framework is demonstrated for a dendrite-free Li-metal anode.  Benefiting from its high surface area (259 m2 g-1) and lightwt. nature with uniformly dispersed lithiophilic MXene nanosheets as Li nucleation sites, the as-formed 3D MG scaffold showcases an ultrahigh Li content (∼92% of the theor. capacity), as well as strong capabilities in suppressing the Li-dendrite formation and accommodating the vol. changes.  Consequently, the MG-based electrode exhibits high Coulombic efficiencies (∼99%) with a record lifespan up to 2700 h and is stable for 230 cycles at an ultrahigh c.d. of 20 mA cm-2.  When coupled with Li4Ti5O12 or sulfur, the MG-Li/Li4Ti5O12 full-cell offers an enhanced capacity of 142 mAh g-1 after 450 cycles, while the MG-Li/sulfur cell delivers an improved rate performance, implying the great potential of this 3D MG framework for building long-lifetime, high-energy-d. batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqSzrSlvgkwrrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhFwEIMYeWUjg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXit1WksbjO&amp;md5=1016f5cb4d18801bddadfb7d9530626a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201808714"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lv, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MXene Aerogel Scaffolds for High-Rate Lithium Metal Anodes</span>. <i>Angew.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MXene Aerogel Scaffolds for High-Rate Lithium Metal Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Xinyue; Lv, Ruijing; Wang, Aoxuan; Guo, Wenqing; Liu, Xingjiang; Luo, Jiayan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">57</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">46</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">15028-15033</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Li metal is considered to be an ultimate anode for metal batteries owing to its extremely high theor. capacity and lowest potential.  However, numerous issues such as short lifespan and infinite vol. expansion caused by the dendrite growth during Li plating/stripping hinder its practical usage.  These challenges become more grievous under high current densities.  Herein, 3-dimensional porous MXene aerogels are proposed as scaffolds for high-rate Li metal anodes using Ti3C2 as an example.  With high metallic electron cond., fast Li ion transport capability, and abundant Li nucleation sites, such scaffolds could deliver high cycling stability and low overpotential at c.d. up to 10 mA cm-2.  High rate performance is also demonstrated in full cells with LiFePO4 as cathodes.  This work provides a new type of scaffolds for Li metal anodes and paves the way for the application of non-graphene 2-dimensional materials toward high energy d. Li metal batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqV_Is_fKOTirVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhFwEIMYeWUjg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhvFOnsr%252FJ&amp;md5=75771ba5360df6a8df0b451626f96575</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201901820"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gong, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Horizontal Growth of Lithium on Parallelly Aligned MXene Layers towards Dendrite-Free Metallic Lithium Anodes</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In 3D printed rGO/CNT microlattice aerogel for a dendrite-free sodium metal anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yan, Jin; Zhi, Gang; Kong, Dezhi; Wang, Hui; Xu, Tingting; Zang, Jinhao; Shen, Weixia; Xu, Junmin; Shi, Yumeng; Dai, Shuge; Li, Xinjian; Wang, Ye</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">38</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">19843-19854</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Uncontrolled dendrite formation induces inferior electrochem. performance in sodium metal and even severe safety issues, resulting in metallic sodium anode being unsuitable for practical applications.  Herein, an artificial reduced graphene oxide/carbon nanotube (rGO/CNT) microlattice aerogel was constructed using three-dimensional (3D) printing technol. and further adopted as a sodium metal host.  With its specially designed architecture, the 3D rGO/CNT microlattice aerogel can effectively reduce the local c.d. and provide abundant active nucleation sites, resulting in homogeneous sodium deposition to overcome the issue of dendrite formation.  As a result, the Na@rGO/CNT microlattice anode enables an areal capacity of 1 mA h cm-2 at 2 mA cm-2 with a small nucleation overpotential of 17.8 mV, with a stable cycling performance for 640 cycles at a high c.d. of 8 mA cm-2.  The exptl. and simulation results show that the improved performance can be attributed to the rational design of the hierarchical rGO/CNT microlattice aerogel with tuned surface kinetics.  Finally, a full battery using a 3D Na@rGO/CNT microlattice as an anode was assembled and delivered a capacity of 67.6 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 100 cycles.  Our results demonstrate that the 3D printed rGO/CNT microlattice aerogel is a promising candidate as a sodium metal host for future generation of sodium metal batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqiCvTS4C3TAbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhFwEIMYeWUjg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsFyku73F&amp;md5=8672c2e0f6eb51f1dafcca6977e02c90</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.0c01157"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kong, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lim, Y.                 10.1021/acsnano.0c01157</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D14%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D9675-9686%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DD.%2BKong%26author%3DY.%2BWang%26author%3DS.%2BHuang%26author%3DB.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BV.%2BLim%26author%3DG.%2BJ.%2BSim%26author%3DY.%2BA.%2BP.%2BValdivia%26author%3DQ.%2BGe%26author%3DH.%2BY.%2BYang%26title%3D3D%2BPrinted%2BCompressible%2BQuasi-Solid-State%2BNickel-Iron%2BBattery%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsnano.0c01157&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.2c01186&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsnano.0c01157&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">3D Printed Compressible Quasi-Solid-State Nickel-Iron Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kong, Dezhi; Wang, Ye; Huang, Shaozhuan; Zhang, Biao; Lim, Yew Von; Sim, Glenn Joey; Valdivia y Alvarado, Pablo; Ge, Qi; Yang, Hui Ying</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9675-9686</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The design of a compressible battery with stable electrochem. performance is extremely important in compression-tolerant and flexible electronics.  While this remains challenging with the current battery manufg. method, the field of 3-dimensional printing offers the possibility of producing free-standing 3-dimensional-printed electrodes with various structural configurations.  Through the simple and scalable strategy, various structural configurations can be produced.  Herein, the authors demonstrate a 3-dimensional-printed quasi-solid-state Ni-Fe battery (QSS-NFB) that shows excellent compressibility, ultrahigh energy d., and superior long-term cycling durability.  Through a rational design and adjustment of chem. components, two electrodes consisting of ultrathin Ni(OH)2 nanosheet array cathode and holey α-Fe2O3 nanorod array anode are achieved with a ultrahigh active material loading over 130 mg/cm3 and excellent compressibility up to 60%.  It is noteworthy that the compressible QSS-NFB demonstrated an excellent cycling stability (~ 91.3% capacity retentions after 10000 cycles) and ultrahigh energy d. (28.1 mWh/cm3 at a power of 10.6 mW cm-3).  This work provides a simple method for producing compression-tolerant energy-storage devices, which are expected to have promising applications in next generation stretchable/wearable electronics.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoXAK3PPFU9q7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljE-phkPIlCBg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhtlegs7bM&amp;md5=d7cc47e3d0a42b6fc9deae2628118b62</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1021/acsaem.0c00309"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Venkatkarthick, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rodthongkum, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pattananuwat, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Vanadium-Based Oxide on Two-Dimensional Vanadium Carbide MXene (V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>x</sub>@V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>) as Cathode for Rechargeable Aqueous Zinc-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Vanadium-Based Oxide on Two-Dimensional Vanadium Carbide MXene (V2Ox@V2CTx) as Cathode for Rechargeable Aqueous Zinc-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Venkatkarthick, Radhakrishnan; Rodthongkum, Nadnudda; Zhang, Xinyu; Wang, Shanmin; Pattananuwat, Prasit; Zhao, Yusheng; Liu, Riping; Qin, Jiaqian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4677-4689</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable aq. zinc-ion batteries (AZIBs) are considered for emerging cutting-edge energy storage technologies as an alternative to the existing nonaq. lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) owing to their inimitable advantages of low-cost materials, high safety, high abundance, and environmental friendliness.  Nevertheless, the key challenges of the AZIBs are mainly due to the development of cathode (pos. electrode) materials.  Here, we report the synthesis of vanadium-based oxides on two-dimensional (2D) vanadium carbide MXene (V2Ox@V2CTx) that can serve as an efficient cathode material for AZIBs.  The vanadium-based oxides could be formed during the high-temp. etching method and by the electrochem. cyclic process.  The prepd. V2Ox@V2CTx electrodes can deliver an ideal rate performance with an av. reversible capacity of about 304 to 84 mAh g-1 at current densities ranging from 0.05 to 2 A g-1, resp.  The obtained results can be comparable to the well-known cathode materials reported for the ZIBs.  Advancing from the characteristic, stable 2D layered structures, V2Ox@V2CTx electrodes could exhibit an improved cycling life with the capacity retention of 81.6% at a rate of 1 A g-1 for about 200 cycles in 1 M ZnSO4 electrolyte.  The prepd. MXene as cathode materials could further pave the way for the development of the advanced zinc ion storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp6hEQit_P0dbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljE-phkPIlCBg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phase Transition Induced Unusual Electrochemical Performance of V2CTX MXene for Aqueous Zinc Hybrid-Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Xinliang; Li, Mian; Yang, Qi; Li, Hongfei; Xu, Hailong; Chai, Zhifang; Chen, Ke; Liu, Zhuoxin; Tang, Zijie; Ma, Longtao; Huang, Zhaodong; Dong, Binbin; Yin, Xiaowei; Huang, Qing; Zhi, Chunyi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nonbattery behavior related phase transition of electrodes is usually not favorable for any batteries because it results in performance degrdn. at all times.  Here, we demonstrate a zinc hybrid-ion battery (ZHIB) with an unusual capacity enhancement even within 18 000 cycles by employing V2CTX MXene as the cathode, enormously differing from all reported counterparts with capacity degrdn. initiated within hundreds of cycles.  The dominated mechanisms are detd. to be MXene delamination and an unexpected phase transition during cycling.  Both the original cathode and secondary deriv. contribute to capacity simultaneously, resulting in the unusual capacity enhancement.  Consequently, the specific capacity of 508 mAh g-1 (highest for all reported aq. zinc-ion batteries) and high energy d. of 386.2 Wh kg-1 are realized.  Also, the quasi-solid-state batteries fabricated can output stably at -20° and in bending, twisting, stabbing, and cutting conditions.  Our work brings an effective approach, i.e., utilizing "unstable" electrode materials, which should usually be avoided, to achieve continuously enhanced performance of a battery.  The idea to use both original and secondary materials for energy storage may be developed to be a general method to achieve extraordinary cycling stability of batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqDyQ745uo347Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljE-phkPIlCBg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXmtVeksw%253D%253D&amp;md5=4e19c0bb49782193befa6de7edb08e04</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1021/acs.jpclett.0c00973"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lei, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hao, Z.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Insight into Adsorption Performance and Mechanism on Efficient Removal of Methylene Blue by Accordion-like V2CTx MXene</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lei, Huan; Hao, Zongdi; Chen, Ke; Chen, Youhu; Zhang, Jianning; Hu, Zhengjie; Song, Yujie; Rao, Pinhua; Huang, Qing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Dyeing wastewater leads to water pollution, and ecol. upset is a crucial issue for the textile industry.  A facile method using two-dimensional transition metal carbides (MXenes) to removal methylene blue (MB) from wastewater is reported.  As previously reported, accordion-like V2CTx MXene was originally demonstrated to have high, spontaneous MB adsorption capacity of 111.11 mg/g, three times greater than that of Ti3C2Tx.  The V2CTx wide lamellar space is certain to have large accommodation for MB.  Electrostatic interaction effects and H-bonding between V2CTx and MB promoted efficient adsorption and provided selectivity between anionic and cationic dyes.  Combined with good reusability, it was anticipated the V2CTx MXene is a promising candidate to remove cationic dyes from textile dyeing wastewater.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpjt5LsqKkc07Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgnnhNqQRcwbA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Perpendicular MXene Arrays with Periodic Interspaces toward Dendrite-Free Lithium Metal Anodes with High-Rate Capabilities</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cao, Zhenjiang; Zhu, Qi; Wang, Shuai; Zhang, Di; Chen, Hao; Du, Zhiguo; Li, Bin; Yang, Shubin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Although lithium metal is an ultimate anode material for lithium-based batteries owing to its high theor. capacity, the uncontrollable dendrites and infinite vol. change assocd. with poor rate capabilities are stagnating its practical applications.  Here, a new type of perpendicular MXene-Li array is developed with tunable MXene walls and const. space in between as anodes for lithium metal batteries.  Such perpendicular MXene arrays possess dual periodic interspaces, i.e., nanometer-scale interspaces in MXene walls and micrometer-scale interspaces between MXene walls.  The former interspaces are favorable for the fast transfer of lithium ions upon stripping and plating, and the latter enables efficiently homogenization of the elec. field, leading to a good high-rate capability up to 20 mA cm-2.  More importantly, the notorious lightning rod effect and vol. change are efficiently inhibited in such perpendicular MXene arrays, giving rise to a dendrite-free lithium anode with a low potential of 25 mV, a high capacity of 2056 mAh g-1, and good cycle stability up to 1700 h.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpCKautkMCoQ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgnnhNqQRcwbA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitFeqtbfP&amp;md5=3febb81e11304660df2728d07878ff16</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201601057"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kong, D.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Boosting the Reversibility of Sodium Metal Anode via Heteroatom-Doped Hollow Carbon Fibers</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zheng, Xueying; Li, Peng; Cao, Zhang; Luo, Wei; Sun, Fazhe; Wang, Zhongqiang; Ding, Bing; Wang, Guoxiu; Huang, Yunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">41</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1902688</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium (Na) metal anodes stand out with their remarkable capacity and natural abundance.  However, the dendritic Na growth, infinite dimensional changes, and low Coulombic efficiency (CE) present key bottlenecks plaguing practical applications.  Here, heteroatom-doped (nitrogen, sulfur) hollow carbon fibers (D-HCF) are rationally synthesized as a nucleation-assisting host to enable a highly reversible Na metal.  The "sodiophilic" functional groups introduced by the heteroatom-doping and large surface area (≈1052 m2 g-1) synchronously contribute to a homogenous plating morphol. with dissipated local c.d.  High "sodiophilicity" of the D-HCF is confirmed by first-principle calcns. and exptl. results, where strong adsorption energy of -3.52 eV with low Na+ nucleation overpotential of 3.2 mV at 0.2 mA cm-2 is realized.  As such, highly reversible plating/stripping is achieved at 1.0 mA cm-2 with av. CE approximating 99.52% over 600 cycles.  The as-assembled Na@D-HCF sym. cells exhibit a prolonged lifetime for 1000 h.  A full-cell paired with Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode further demonstrates stable electrochem. behavior for 200 cycles at 1 C along with excellent rate performance (102 mAh g-1 at 5 C).  The results clearly show the effectiveness of the D-HCF in manipulating Na+ deposition and thus the significance of nucleation control in realizing dendrite-free metal anodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqxU47jxzXqPLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liu5GrTh3h3-Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhsFyks73I&amp;md5=09c535e93691cd88ae75e0ed3125d9f3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1039/C9TA05176G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Matios, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tin nanoparticles embedded in a carbon buffer layer as preferential nucleation sites for stable sodium metal anodes</span>. <i>J. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>7</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">23747</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">23755</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tin nanoparticles embedded in a carbon buffer layer as preferential nucleation sites for stable sodium metal anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Huan; Matios, Edward; Wang, Chuanlong; Luo, Jianmin; Lu, Xuan; Hu, Xiaofei; Zhang, Yiwen; Li, Weiyang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">41</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">23747-23755</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium (Na) metal is one of the most appealing anode materials for grid-scale energy storage systems owing to the high earth abundance and low cost of Na resources.  Nevertheless, the implementation of the Na metal anode is hindered by two primary issues assocd. with Na dendrite growth and vol. expansion, resulting in low coulombic efficiency and poor cycle life.  Herein we present a facile and scalable method to synthesize tin (Sn) nanoparticles (NPs) that are uniformly embedded within a carbon network (denoted as Sn@C composite), which can address the two issues simultaneously.  Specifically, Sn NPs can serve as preferential nucleation sites to guide Na nucleation and thereby lower the Na deposition overpotential, while the carbon network can act as a buffer layer to effectively minimize the vol. change and alleviate the exfoliation of Sn NPs over repeated cycles.  Consequently, high-capacity Na anodes can be realized with long-term reversibility and stability.  Moreover, a room-temp. Na-sulfur battery based on the Sn@C composite as an anode coupled with com. sodium sulfide as a cathode was demonstrated to have significantly improved electrochem. performance.  We believe that this work provides a new pathway for designing high-energy Na metal batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpziV1rZJnferVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liu5GrTh3h3-Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXht1ykurrJ&amp;md5=fb79c5a13103ba0518a642894641743c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2019.152403"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub>x</sub> MXene/graphene nanocomposites: Synthesis and application in electrochemical energy storage</span>. <i>J.                 10.1016/j.jallcom.2019.152403</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D815%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D152403%26journal%3DJ.%2BAlloys%2BCompd.%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DJ.%2BYu%26author%3DD.%2BGuo%26author%3DZ.%2BLi%26author%3DY.%2BSu%26title%3DTi3C2Tx%2BMXene%252Fgraphene%2Bnanocomposites%253A%2BSynthesis%2Band%2Bapplication%2Bin%2Belectrochemical%2Benergy%2Bstorage%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jallcom.2019.152403&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsnano.2c01186&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jallcom.2019.152403&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ti3C2Tx MXene/graphene nanocomposites: Synthesis and application in electrochemical energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yanyue; Yu, Jiaxin; Guo, Dongfang; Li, Zijiong; Su, Yanjie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">815</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">152403</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JALCEU</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0925-8388</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review is given.  Similar to graphene, 2-dimensional (2D) transition metal carbides and nitrides (MXenes) have been demonstrated great potential in the electrochem. energy storage owing to their excellent hydrophilicity and cond., large specific capacitance and excellent electrochem. performance, etc.  The combination of MXene and graphene can effectively prevent the restacking of graphene and MXene, which greatly improve the sp. surface area and specific capacity of MXene and graphene.  However, the large-scale prodn. of MXene/graphene materials through low-cost and simple synthetic route is a big challenge.  Here, we present recent synthesis methods of Ti3C2 MXene/graphene composites and the related mechanisms.  Subsequently, the progress in the energy storage applications of the composites are summarized, including supercapacitors, Li-ion batteries, Li-S batteries, etc.  The current existing problem and prospects of the MXene/graphene composites are discussed, which will provide a ref. for the design and prepn. of high-performance MXene-based energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp3OldPCN-Px7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liu5GrTh3h3-Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhvV2ktrvN&amp;md5=2b8099ca67d4c399bc2ddcc41bcc2643</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1039/D0TA01853H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">An, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Atomic-scale identification of influencing factors of sodium dendrite growth on different current collectors</span>. <i>J. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>8</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">10199</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">10205</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Atomic-scale identification of influencing factors of sodium dendrite growth on different current collectors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Mengting; Sun, Bing; Ao, Zhimin; An, Taicheng; Wang, Guoxiu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">20</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10199-10205</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">To design high-performance and safe Na metal anodes for rechargeable Na-metal batteries, the dendrite-growth mechanisms during the Na electroplating process need to be fully understood.  Here, a d. functional theory (DFT) insight is provided into essential mechanisms assocd. with Na dendrite formation on different current collectors, such as Cu, Al, and single wall carbon nanotubes (SWCNTs).  The adsorption behavior is investigated of Na atoms on SWCNTs, Cu (111) surfaces, and Al (111) surfaces and further compared the stability of Na dimers.  The "sodiophilic" properties and electronic configuration of Cu, Al, and SWCNTs were evaluated.  Meanwhile, the electron transfer and the stability of Na dimers were estd.  For the adsorption of a single Na atom, the SWCNT, Cu and Al performed well with adsorption energies of -2.15, -2.93 and -2.24 eV, resp.  However, the Na dimer was not energetically favorable to form on SWCNTs.  Based on Hirshfeld at. charges and electron d. distribution, the stable electron configuration of the SWCNT was found to play a crit. role in dispersing Na adatoms.  In addn., the vacancy defects in the SWCNT induced better "sodiophilic" properties and inhibited dendrite growth.  The results unraveled the possible mechanisms underlying dendritic electrodeposition of Na on SWCNTs, Cu and Al current collectors, indicating that SWCNTs can be a promising current collector to develop dendrite-free Na metal anodes for safe Na-metal batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrjLzrmg_ejFrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liu5GrTh3h3-Q"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly Self-Healable 3D Microsupercapacitor with MXene-Graphene Composite Aerogel</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yue, Yang; Liu, Nishuang; Ma, Yanan; Wang, Siliang; Liu, Weijie; Luo, Cheng; Zhang, Hang; Cheng, Feng; Rao, Jiangyu; Hu, Xiaokang; Su, Jun; Gao, Yihua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4224-4232</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High-performance microsupercapacitors (MSCs) with three-dimensional (3D) structure provide an effective approach to improve the ability of energy storage.  Because the electrodes with 3D structure are generally easily destroyed under mech. deformation in practical applications, we fabricated a self-healable 3D MSC consisting of MXene (Ti3C2Tx)-graphene (reduced graphene oxide, rGO) composite aerogel electrode by wrapping it with a self-healing polyurethane as an outer shell.  The MXene-rGO composite aerogel combining large sp. surface area of rGO and high cond. of the MXene can not only prevent the self-restacking of the lamella structure but also resist the poor oxidization of MXene to a degree.  The MSC based on a 3D MXene-rGO aerogel delivers a large area specific capacitance of 34.6 mF cm-2 at a scan rate of 1 mV s-1 and an outstanding cycling performance with a capacitance retention up to 91% over 15,000 cycles.  The 3D MSC presents an excellent self-healing ability with specific capacitance retention of 81.7% after the fifth healing.  The prepn. of this self-healable 3D MSC can provide a method for designing and manufg. next-generation long-life multifunctional electronic devices further to meet the requirements of sustainable development.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoaeIa2GHEyLrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhulFZoXciwGA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXnsF2kuro%253D&amp;md5=d7c70164c8e2bf6fba88da6a51d0b90d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref50"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">50</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit50" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2017.10.050"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, M.-S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">In-situ electron microscopy observation of electrochemical sodium plating and stripping dynamics on carbon nanofiber current collectors</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>42</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">122</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">128</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In-situ electron microscopy observation of electrochemical sodium plating and stripping dynamics on carbon nanofiber current collectors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Xuke; Zhao, Longze; Li, Pei; Zhang, Qiaobao; Wang, Ming-Sheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">42</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium metal holds promise as the ultimate anode for high-energy-d. Na battery systems.  Recent progress has been made in terms of rational design of nanostructured 3D current collectors for dendrite-free Na deposition with limited dimensional changes during cycling.  However, crit. information such as Na nucleation and growth behavior on these hosts remains elusive.  Herein, by using amorphous carbon nanofibers (CNF) as a current collector, we present the first nanoscale-resoln. observation of electrochem. Na plating/stripping dynamics via in situ electron microscopies.  With the use of solid electrolyte, Na metal was found to grow and dissolve reversibly as nano/micro-particles at all the possible locations around indiviual CNFs and even throughout their network.  Notably, inter-fiber Na ion transport was exptl. confirmed, which enables more homogeneous Na deposition deep into the network interior without interfacing the electrolyte; this would be crucial for dendrite-free Na plating, esp. in all-solid-state Na batteries.  In addn., through a delicately designed in-situ expt., the CNF interior exhibited a superior Na capacity compared to its graphitized counterpart.  Thus, owning to both exterior and interior Na storage of each fiber, CNFs could be a promising host material for building rechargeable composite Na metal anodes with ultrahigh capacity.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq82IERYaX-mbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhulFZoXciwGA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhsleks7fO&amp;md5=c37d5edb55dc57bb59ceac426956a14e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1017/S1431927621009624"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Misra, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Boebinger, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mathis, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Naguib, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gogotsi, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Unocic, R.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">In Situ TEM Investigation of Lithium Intercalation in Ti<sub>3</sub>C<sub>2</sub>T<sub>x</sub> MXenes for Energy Storage Applications</span>. <i>Microsc.                         cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Bottom-Up Lithium Growth Triggered by Interfacial Activity Gradient on Porous Framework for Lithium-Metal Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yun, Jonghyeok; Park, Beom-Kyeong; Won, Eun-Seo; Choi, Seung Hyun; Kang, Hyon Chol; Kim, Jung Ho; Park, Min-Sik; Lee, Jong-Won</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3108-3114</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AELCCP</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Three-dimensional (3D) porous frameworks have attracted considerable interest as lithium-metal electrodes for next-generation rechargeable batteries.  The high surface areas and large pore vols. of 3D frameworks are beneficial for reducing local current densities and suppressing vol. changes.  However, uneven Li plating on top of the framework electrode (top growth) has yet to be resolved.  To enable the bottom-up Li growth while suppressing the top growth, herein, a rational design is proposed of 3D framework electrodes with an interfacial activity gradient (IAG) based on a kinetics-based mechanistic anal.  A simulation demonstrates that an IAG design promotes the bottom-up Li growth, which is exptl. proven using model architectures.  The IAG-Cu framework shows considerable improvements in morphol. stability and reversibility during high-capacity Li storage, compared to the Cu framework with a uniform interfacial activity.  This work provides fundamental insight into the design of 3D frameworks to boost the cycling stability of Li-metal batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpkzqfchJQpxLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhulFZoXciwGA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhslSqt7%252FL&amp;md5=0a8ecb6cc70efa922c11ca2601628986</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref53'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">53</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit53" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201901839"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Versatile N-Doped MXene Ink for Printed Electrochemical Energy Storage Application</span>. <i>Adv.
